  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_04c90831-f780-4527-a393-fd7d66c9b5fe'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_2799589771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2799589771" />
    <a title="Christa Maurice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2911205-christa-maurice"><img alt="Christa Maurice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430856086p2/2911205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2799589771?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christa Maurice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christa Maurice" href="/user/show/2911205-christa-maurice">Christa Maurice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/43510351-winter-world">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2799589771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2820715901681753670">Written like a screenplay, all talking heads with no chemistry between the characters. I'm not going to believe that the two main characters are falling in love just because the author tells me they are. The male MC is a total Mary Sue too. He received his doctorate in biochem on the same day as he got one in medicine. He can analyze people better than a psychiatrist. His only flaw is that he thinks people are better than they are.<br/><br/>I suppose he leaps tall buildings and travels faster than a speed</span>
  <span id="freeText2820715901681753670" style="display:none">Written like a screenplay, all talking heads with no chemistry between the characters. I'm not going to believe that the two main characters are falling in love just because the author tells me they are. The male MC is a total Mary Sue too. He received his doctorate in biochem on the same day as he got one in medicine. He can analyze people better than a psychiatrist. His only flaw is that he thinks people are better than they are.<br /><br />I suppose he leaps tall buildings and travels faster than a speeding bullet in his spare time. I'll save my reading time for Elizabeth Moon who writes compelling characters in believable situations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2820715901681753670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2799071270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6326096661906225825">Very meh. It felt like an attempt to cross Enders Game with the Martian, but it fell flat. I honestly can't even remember anyone's names from the novel only a few weeks past reading it. The two main characters are a male who is a super genius, and ends up being a great leader, statistician, public speaker, and overall a Mary Sue coupled with a female who is an astronaut and crew leader but ends up being nothing more than a love interest following the male around. How great it could have been if </span>
  <span id="freeText6326096661906225825" style="display:none">Very meh. It felt like an attempt to cross Enders Game with the Martian, but it fell flat. I honestly can't even remember anyone's names from the novel only a few weeks past reading it. The two main characters are a male who is a super genius, and ends up being a great leader, statistician, public speaker, and overall a Mary Sue coupled with a female who is an astronaut and crew leader but ends up being nothing more than a love interest following the male around. How great it could have been if he had been kept the awkward nervous genius and she the decisive strategic leader. Their chemistry could have grown from their mutual strengths instead of his rescuing her and her following him around like a loyal puppy.<br /><br />The sci-fi elements weren't bad and the action was written well enough, but I couldn't connect with either of the mains and kept rolling my eyes when the male proved to be great at everything he touched.</span>

<div id="review_2735629979" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2735629979" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7182738-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546466781p2/7182738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735629979?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/7182738-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/43510351-winter-world">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7182738-mel?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735629979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9122341633326107123">I'm aware I'm odd woman out...I don't want to be! I want to be in the group of A.G. Riddle lovers!<br/>It's not Riddle, it's me, and that's obvious by the author's hordes of fans.<br/><br/>My first A.G. Riddle so I have no connection to Riddle, no fond memories of previous books, and am out of my lane. As many sci-fi movies that I watch, one would think I'd like sci-fi books, but not so. I've read several sci-fi novels this year that were all highly recommended, award-winners, but nothing notable. I usually su</span>
  <span id="freeText9122341633326107123" style="display:none">I'm aware I'm odd woman out...I don't want to be! I want to be in the group of A.G. Riddle lovers!<br>It's not Riddle, it's me, and that's obvious by the author's hordes of fans.<br><br>My first A.G. Riddle so I have no connection to Riddle, no fond memories of previous books, and am out of my lane. As many sci-fi movies that I watch, one would think I'd like sci-fi books, but not so. I've read several sci-fi novels this year that were all highly recommended, award-winners, but nothing notable. I usually suffer through them with high hopes that deflate the closer I get to the ending of each contender. <br><br>Why I didn't care for this? It didn't snag me; it didn't spark anything, and I thought the ho-hum sexual tension was a routine attempt at probable conflict. I'm willing to sacrifice the literary vein, as far as stellar writing goes (npi), but the exchange should be for an exciting, captivating, hold-on-to-your-butts plot with characters memorable beyond 10 seconds after you close the book. I want my mainstream fiction to instantly hook me with the story being equally driven by inventive plot and promising characters. I <i>do</i> think the plot will eventually show potential (because it seems to hint at something that has been done very successfully before). Unfortunately, the characters I found to be little more than sketchy introductions that didn't evolve enough out of their embryonic stage to be engaging. It's the first in a series--I know-- but you have to want to come back and check in with characters you like. Dr James Sinclair's stint in prison for mysterious reasons didn't do enough to whet my appetite; his female counterpart, Dr Emma Matthews, was just simply 2D. She's smart, co-dependent, has deteriorating bone mass due to her long stay in space, and has a gummy bear for a heart. But, maybe Einstein's time-slowing effects of acceleration and gravity also make the heart fall for whatever or whoever shares various high-flying spacecraft. <br><br>The story is told from both space travelers perspectives, and though it adds some switch in the narration, Riddle hasn't solved the age-old problem of having different characters speak from one head, especially characters that seem still in the developmental stages. For an apocalyptic thriller, this just whimpers, while the author seems to spend more time writing about trivial personal events than the looming wipeout of planet Earth. <br> <br>Unless the author has come up with something truly unique or petrifying as the adversary...pass my pillow. But again, I think there is a hint of potential. Without giving away anything, I had some <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/70535.2001_A_Space_Odyssey__Space_Odyssey___1_" title="2001 A Space Odyssey (Space Odyssey, #1) by Arthur C. Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">2001: A Space Odyssey</a> deja vu moments. Geometry does not behave in space as we know it to do on Earth. <br><br>Regarding <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/285746.The_Anvil_of_Ice__The_Winter_of_the_World___1_" title="The Anvil of Ice (The Winter of the World, #1) by Michael Scott Rohan" rel="nofollow noopener"> Winter World #1</a> ... I wish these characters all the best with their space exploits as they endeavor to save the world. I'd probably like the movie version <b>if</b>: this book #1 comprised just the first 15-20 minutes of the film; the special effects were mind-blowing; the characters were dimensional, interesting and believable; there was more back story to add the desire to hang on through the <i>series-to-come</i>; and if the plot moved with more intensity and speed. As it is, Winter World #1 felt like a couple of chapters quickly written and stretched into a book. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551576836ra/27145413.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9122341633326107123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13891003245364411001" style="display:none">Not an enjoyable read, and quite poorly written. I felt like I was forcing myself to finish the latter third of the book just so I could move on to reading something else as quickly as possible. I doubt any other book includes the word “drone” quite as many times as this one either. <br /><br />The book is presented through two main characters, a Male know it all with apparently no flaws, and a female astronaut. I agree with many of the other reviews on here, the female lead turned from a strong interesting character into the whiny girlfriend in a short space of time. I won’t be rushing to read the sequel as the plot really wasn’t entertaining enough. Too many strange time jumps and inexplicable plot holes (building 9 identical space ships in a few months when we’re told there are no resources left on a frozen earth and everybody is starving to death for one). Avoid. </span>

<div id="review_3176802338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3176802338" />
    <a title="Pat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407123-pat"><img alt="Pat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591983365p2/7407123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3176802338?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pat" href="/user/show/7407123-pat">Pat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3176802338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8827064165388505145">In a startling about face it looks like I am the odd one out for actually liking this book (even though it rated quite highly). After our months of fires, heatwaves and years of drought I found this story, set in the very near future, about the earth facing a sudden ice age and thought it would make a nice change. I really didn’t know what to expect and found myself fully immersed in - ta da, science fiction. This is not a genre I read widely and certainly not lately. Which might explain why I e</span>
  <span id="freeText8827064165388505145" style="display:none">In a startling about face it looks like I am the odd one out for actually liking this book (even though it rated quite highly). After our months of fires, heatwaves and years of drought I found this story, set in the very near future, about the earth facing a sudden ice age and thought it would make a nice change. I really didn’t know what to expect and found myself fully immersed in - ta da, science fiction. This is not a genre I read widely and certainly not lately. Which might explain why I enjoyed it. My expectations were not high, I’m not a fan of sci-fi, so I don’t have a lot to compare this to.<br /><br />Notwithstanding the fact that the main characters seemed too good to be true and the science may or may not have been plausible (I really don’t know) the actual premise was different. The whole book was different to anything I have read. In my view that is a huge plus after many very derivative and predictable thrillers.<br /><br />This was the first book in a trilogy. The earth has been inexplicably getting colder and humanity is under threat as people move to warmer places, places below sea level (i.e. Death Valley)! Anywhere they can get to. NASA has launched some probes via the International Space Station (ISS) to measure the sun’s radiation. They find that the whole area of space around the earth is receiving much less solar radiation than normal. And the ice continues to advance. One of the probes spots a strange artefact before it is destroyed. This ‘thing’ just shouldn’t be there. Then the ISS itself it pelted by debris and is effectively destroyed. There is one survivor, Commander Emma Matthews.<br /><br />Meanwhile federal agents spring Dr James Sinclair from a federal penitentiary. He is some kind of genius - a medical doctor who has never practised but is also qualified in biomechanical engineering and ended up being some kind of robotocist guru. We don’t know why he was in prison until much later. He is rushed to NASA which is mounting a hasty space mission to study the artefact and to try and work out how and why the sun is being blocked from earth. On the way they detour slightly to rescue Emma who is still drifting around in a damaged escape module from the ISS.<br /><br /> Yes, I know it’s all very unbelievable but it was a heck of a story, at least for one not accustomed to the genre. Most of the narration is first person from Emma and James and much of the action takes place in space. I should probably stop there. As for the detractors, I’m not sure why the criticism. In sci-fi as in horror pretty much anything goes. While it may not have been plausible it certainly hung together and made sense within the narrative. Anyway, I really enjoyed the journey and I’m now off to get book 2.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8827064165388505145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14354910546082612713" style="display:none">This is a good book, but it didn't stay with me. <span id="freeTextContainer17001734860130337839"><strong>Dual first person telling not showing.</strong><br/><br/>5 stars for imagination.<br/>1 star for style.<br/>Reads like a high school kid wrote it. There are two protagonists and the writing annoyingly shifts between their first person narrative. Their voices are very similar. The grammar is mostly okay, but the style is atrocious. There are many four word sentences and the dialogue lacks nuance and depth. Perhaps Riddle’s worst work.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2926216473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer497099066309874963">I really enjoyed this one. It has the making of a Hollywood blockbuster. I kept seeing the movie in my mind as I was listening to the audiobook!<br/><br/>It follows two astronauts, Emma and James as they attempt to save the world and discover what is bringing about a new ice-age.<br/><br/>Winter World<br/>I thought it was great, lots of action, adventure, and romance… Ok so I didn’t like the romance so much. I thought it was extremely corny. But overall it was a great book!<br/><br/>It was non-stop something happening. I enjoyed </span>
  <span id="freeText497099066309874963" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this one. It has the making of a Hollywood blockbuster. I kept seeing the movie in my mind as I was listening to the audiobook!<br /><br />It follows two astronauts, Emma and James as they attempt to save the world and discover what is bringing about a new ice-age.<br /><br />Winter World<br />I thought it was great, lots of action, adventure, and romance… Ok so I didn’t like the romance so much. I thought it was extremely corny. But overall it was a great book!<br /><br />It was non-stop something happening. I enjoyed the writing and the characters.<br /><br />One thing that I didn’t like was the predictability. I pretty much figured out all the main “OMG WHAT DID HE DO? JUST TELL US ALREADY!!” twists straight away, so I was bummed about the big revelation. It was just so predictable. Along with the absolutely stupidly corny romance – this is where it lost the wow factor for me and I deducted a star.<br /><br />However, overall a great read. Would make a fabulous movie, kinda like deep impact meets the day after tomorrow, meets independence day crossed with the matrix. I enjoyed it very much.<br /><br /><b>What did I think of the audio version?</b><br />Yes I loved it! The narrators were excellent and it was like a movie in my mind!<br /><br /><b>Would I recommend Winter World?</b><br />Yes it was a fun read! Very intelligent and thought provoking in some parts and all out fun adventure in others. I didn’t buy the romance at all, but thankfully that was not what I was particularly after in this one.<br /><br />If you like action-packed end-of-the-world books, this will be right up your alley.<br /><br /><i>I purchased Winter World at my own expense on audible.com</i><br /><br />For more reviews check out my:<br /><a href="http://www.melsbookshelf.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a><br /> <a href="http://www.instagram.com/mels_book_shelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br /> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/melsbookshelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br /> <a href="http://www.facebook.com/melsbookshelfAU" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2800192794?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/4348181-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/43510351-winter-world">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4348181-misty?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2800192794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6258868793554722562">So, I’m a self-professed fan of post-apocalyptic lit, but I prefer it without zombies, monsters or “nerdy” elements that make me feel like an outsider. I was surprised, then, to find that I actually LOVED this book, in spite of the sometimes lengthy intellectual passages that explicated aspects of astronomy and space travel. What impressed me most was the character development. Author A.G. Riddle has breathed life into a variety of personas, each unique, interesting and, most importantly, believ</span>
  <span id="freeText6258868793554722562" style="display:none">So, I’m a self-professed fan of post-apocalyptic lit, but I prefer it without zombies, monsters or “nerdy” elements that make me feel like an outsider. I was surprised, then, to find that I actually LOVED this book, in spite of the sometimes lengthy intellectual passages that explicated aspects of astronomy and space travel. What impressed me most was the character development. Author A.G. Riddle has breathed life into a variety of personas, each unique, interesting and, most importantly, believable. Additionally, I was completely engaged, from page one through the edge-of-your-seat conclusion—so much so, in fact, that I hated to turn the final page! I was, however, thrilled to discover that there’s a sequel in the works. <br /><br />When perusing other reviews, I noticed that there’s some criticism about the validity of some of the facts presented. I honestly have no idea how valid those comments are. I just accepted what was written at face value and enjoyed the ride. <br /><br />If you long for a good story, with characters you will love, definitely add this to your “need-to-read” list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6258868793554722562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10974198336057741019">This wasn’t a roller coaster for me. It was a cliff dive. <br/><br/>What started as a strong 4 storyline with a bit of not unexpected caricature and cliche writing devolved and then plunged into unremitting male ego stoking, a wildly non-credible nominal female co-lead character who was nothing but weepy cotton batting and self-deprecation (a NASA astronaut commander??) who existed only as a prop for the expert-in-everything glorified good-guy bad-boy male lead, and a thinly supported space drama plot. <br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText10974198336057741019" style="display:none">This wasn’t a roller coaster for me. It was a cliff dive. <br /><br />What started as a strong 4 storyline with a bit of not unexpected caricature and cliche writing devolved and then plunged into unremitting male ego stoking, a wildly non-credible nominal female co-lead character who was nothing but weepy cotton batting and self-deprecation (a NASA astronaut commander??) who existed only as a prop for the expert-in-everything glorified good-guy bad-boy male lead, and a thinly supported space drama plot. <br /><br />I stopped when it was evident that this is, for me, a 1 star read with sorrowfully good potential, and when I was trying to distract myself from the aggravation and disappointment of the actual book by imagining to which authors I would like to entrust this apocalyptic sci fi plot that I really would have liked to read. At that point I woke up to the teeth gritting stance I was taking to get through it and sent it to the DNF pile. <br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13448605879077773059">I tend to gravitate toward certain genres during certain seasons. Spring, for example, is a time of hope, and so it requires the hope-filled literature of science fiction. Finding good science fiction, though, isn't easy. That's because good science fiction builds believable worlds and creates characters we care about while also blowing our minds with science and technology that's almost indistinguishable from magic.   <span id="freeText13448605879077773059" style="display:none">I tend to gravitate toward certain genres during certain seasons. Spring, for example, is a time of hope, and so it requires the hope-filled literature of science fiction. Finding good science fiction, though, isn't easy. That's because good science fiction builds believable worlds and creates characters we care about while also blowing our minds with science and technology that's almost indistinguishable from magic. Talk about a tall order!<br /><br />Winter World is good science fiction. I raced through it on my Kindle, and the second I crossed the finish line I was met with the option to pre-order the sequel, which I did. Here's the thing, though: I never do that! I never buy a book before it's been out for a while, and people have had a chance to review it. I'm cautious that way.<br /><br />But with Winter World, I threw caution to the solar winds. Now I'm counting down the days until I can once again lose myself in some good science fiction!</span>

  <span id="freeText12664013642979300849" style="display:none">This is a really poor book. There is no depth to the plot, and no tension between the characters. Everyone is perfectly reasonable and of course very clever with the hero being a "genius". The "love" story is not credible, you get no sense of the 2 characters having joy in each other. The hero falls in love with her practically from her photo alone (yawn) which exudes a special "energy" (yawn yawn). Throughout the book in fact, the point of Emma was hard to fathom. She added nothing to the story not even romantic tension. I wonder did the publishers insist on a love interest?<br /><br />I've read the Atlantic Gene trilogy which while certainly not great literature is a very entertaining and absorbing read. But this. It's really just a flat relating in very broad strokes of stuff that happens. No detail to give it credibility and weight. No real obstacles to the ... end objectives. <br /><br />Just all very dull. If you are dithering on whether to read it, I say skip it.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2703363358" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10778893010370278852">Sci fi thriller with a frozen Earth and invaders from Space<br/><br/>James Sinclair is a medical doctor and a bioengineer specializing in robotics. He is a one-of-a-kind genius who also happens to be in Federal prison for the rest of his life.<br/><br/>Emma Matthews is a geneticist and a crew commander of the International Space Station.<br/><br/>Both become valuable contributors on a dangerous mission to find out what's blocking the Sun and throwing Earth into the next Ice Age.<br/><br/>I was surprised by this book. I guess I didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText10778893010370278852" style="display:none">Sci fi thriller with a frozen Earth and invaders from Space<br /><br />James Sinclair is a medical doctor and a bioengineer specializing in robotics. He is a one-of-a-kind genius who also happens to be in Federal prison for the rest of his life.<br /><br />Emma Matthews is a geneticist and a crew commander of the International Space Station.<br /><br />Both become valuable contributors on a dangerous mission to find out what's blocking the Sun and throwing Earth into the next Ice Age.<br /><br />I was surprised by this book. I guess I didn't read the blurb thoroughly enough. I thought this book was mainly going to be post-apocalyptic about the Earth freezing over. And it was - but that takes a backseat to the space saga. Probably at least 2/3 of this story takes place in Space or preparing to go into Space.<br /><br />I was okay with the sci fi space story. I enjoy these types of books also. The book was well written and had plenty of brave, selfless characters. The story was full of "tech talk" as the intrepid adventurers strive to save Earth.<br /><br />Another thing I didn't notice was that this is the first book in a two-part series. It had a fine ending and could be a standalone in my opinion. But a second book THE SOLAR WAR is due out June 25, 2019.<br /><br />If you enjoyed the disaster movies THE CORE and ARMAGEDDON, I am sure you'll enjoy this tale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10778893010370278852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3400056141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer861174374180914885">Review for the whole series. <br/><br/>This was my first Riddle experience, after hearing about his works for a long time. Nothing spectacular... but nothing particularly horrific either. I try to not judge books based on the highest peaks of the genre they belong to. I judge them on what they claim to be and how effectively and cleanly they achieve whatever they aim for. I gave this series 3 stars all throughout because I think that's what it deserves. It's nothing deep, nothing world-changing, nothing s</span>
  <span id="freeText861174374180914885" style="display:none">Review for the whole series. <br /><br />This was my first Riddle experience, after hearing about his works for a long time. Nothing spectacular... but nothing particularly horrific either. I try to not judge books based on the highest peaks of the genre they belong to. I judge them on what they claim to be and how effectively and cleanly they achieve whatever they aim for. I gave this series 3 stars all throughout because I think that's what it deserves. It's nothing deep, nothing world-changing, nothing so stupendously good that I've put my life on hold for it. It's just some fast-paced, action forward SF series, with a handful of one-dimensional characters who at least have the decency to be consistent all the way through. I use this type of fiction as a break between other works that I'm reading, particularly if I'm deep into history or something like that, and I see massive value in that. In books like these, the world-building is not the problem: I actually think some of the ideas are decent and I always enjoy discovering another literary Universe. It's the dialogue that kills me, and the incessant interjections of the narrator into the story, feeling the need to make things way, way too clear for the reader. In any case, it's good enough for a fast read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="861174374180914885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3438420377?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim Kaso" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim Kaso" href="/user/show/39507342-kim-kaso">Kim Kaso</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39507342-kim-kaso?shelf=2020lor5000">2020lor5000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39507342-kim-kaso?shelf=2020l-l60">2020l-l60</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39507342-kim-kaso?shelf=coffee-books2020">coffee-books2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3438420377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6929688995100327720">In our current situation (C-19 & hunkering down at home) I am more careful about what I read, as my mood can darken more easily, especially while I recover from surgery. Dystopian novels can be a challenge, as can be books involving disease & pandemics. I am choosing to read reliable authors for comfort & mood improvement along with the books that are more challenging to my emotional health. I was leery of this book, but fell into reading it after I read the back cover & found myself 50 pages in</span>
  <span id="freeText6929688995100327720" style="display:none">In our current situation (C-19 &amp; hunkering down at home) I am more careful about what I read, as my mood can darken more easily, especially while I recover from surgery. Dystopian novels can be a challenge, as can be books involving disease &amp; pandemics. I am choosing to read reliable authors for comfort &amp; mood improvement along with the books that are more challenging to my emotional health. I was leery of this book, but fell into reading it after I read the back cover &amp; found myself 50 pages in when l looked up. I was so pleased to find myself in a book where the government is actually doing something about an existential crisis, is recruiting &amp; trusting the best minds to deal with it, and is fully supporting, funding, &amp; trusting them to do what is best. People are dedicated, willing to sacrifice, putting others before themselves, trying to do what is right for the greater good. It is the polar opposite of what is happening too often currently, and it is refreshing. I tore through this book and thoroughly enjoyed the ride. I love Emma, James, and their colleagues, highly recommend this book, and look forward to the rest of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6929688995100327720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2731685337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2731685337" />
    <a title="Karen Brooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2382210-karen-brooks"><img alt="Karen Brooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450143415p2/2382210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2731685337?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Brooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Brooks" href="/user/show/2382210-karen-brooks">Karen Brooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2731685337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5595323059333033933">Having read and thoroughly enjoyed A.G. Riddle’s Pandemic series, I couldn’t wait to read his latest, Winter World. Not only do I love the visceral thrill of eschatological narratives and their exploration of geo-political machinations as well as emotional and psychological trauma and challenges of facing the end of the world as we know it and how people react, but the notion of the earth becoming a winter wasteland (and the reasons behind this) were fascinating to me - very Day After Tomorrow-e</span>
  <span id="freeText5595323059333033933" style="display:none">Having read and thoroughly enjoyed A.G. Riddle’s Pandemic series, I couldn’t wait to read his latest, Winter World. Not only do I love the visceral thrill of eschatological narratives and their exploration of geo-political machinations as well as emotional and psychological trauma and challenges of facing the end of the world as we know it and how people react, but the notion of the earth becoming a winter wasteland (and the reasons behind this) were fascinating to me - very Day After Tomorrow-esque.<br /><br />This tale of the earth’s rapid change from varied climate and where power is concentrated in familiar regions to one where mass immigration from First World centres to formerly third world countries is told from two points of view. The first is that of an astronaut/scientist and commander, Emma, and a brilliant doctor and roboticist (among other things) James, who commences the book in a federal prison. The way Riddle tells the story of earth’s epic struggle to survive an attack that will destroy all life is at once personalized through these two characters and the relationships they form with their families, colleagues and each other, but also far-reaching. He cleverly keeps the pace moving by leaping the story forward and avoiding what some sci-fi narratives do (albeit some do it very well), bogging the reader down in extraneous scientific detail that show the author’s grasp of technical complexities as opposed to serving the story. We are given some of the science and for this Luddite, it appears to work. But it is the story that captures you - as well as demands you suspend your disbelief - as James and Emma and the brilliant people they work with fight to battle an alien enemy no-one predicted and who is ruthless in the extreme. <br /><br />My only mild reservations are that James and Emma are so damn courageous and amazing. James is like the nerd’s James Bond personified but with the ability to grow and change - for the better (even when he’s practically perfect in every way). Emma, through great tragedy and personal hardship is also a geek Mary Poppins - intelligent, focused, self-sacrificing and lovely. I just wish there were more people Iike Emma and James in real life. As it is, I’ll have to wait for the sequel to find out where their battle and the dangerous adventures that ensue lead. Looking forward to it!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5595323059333033933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2734698440" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Adrian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37887132-adrian"><img alt="Adrian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418442540p2/37887132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781980033134" href="/book/show/44152153-winter-world">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37887132-adrian?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37887132-adrian?shelf=2019-read-in-2019">2019-read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37887132-adrian?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37887132-adrian?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734698440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15507114709285216710">This book starts with an interesting concept – the world is cooling instead of warming.<br/><br/>Ok, so I don’t really get nitpicky about books and try to enjoy them for what they are – merely entertainment. But there was just something about this one that bothered me. I can’t really put a finger on it and maybe I didn’t fully understand things but there were too many holes and seemingly-missing-storylines. For one, the relationship between the two main characters was weird, rushed, and just convenient. A</span>
  <span id="freeText15507114709285216710" style="display:none">This book starts with an interesting concept – the world is cooling instead of warming.<br /><br />Ok, so I don’t really get nitpicky about books and try to enjoy them for what they are – merely entertainment. But there was just something about this one that bothered me. I can’t really put a finger on it and maybe I didn’t fully understand things but there were too many holes and seemingly-missing-storylines. For one, the relationship between the two main characters was weird, rushed, and just convenient. A lot of “staring” as one reviewer points out. The author does not portray the awesome-former-commander of the ISS as a strong competent woman. She seems kind of weak and lovestruck. There are other holes in which these space travelers just happen to jet off from Earth and end up in the Asteroid belt. Something like that would take so much time that I would think the author would at least mention that (or research that). Speaking of space travelers, all of these non-astronauts quickly and easily become space voyagers without much training or rigor of going through this type of environment/experience. Plus, the main character is so smart that he just figures out all of the enemy’s moves and locations. These super scientists seem to make complex drones of all sorts in a matter of minutes with no issues. And the plotline kind of seemed predictable. There wasn’t enough explanation of the actual turmoil and death count that the earth would be experiencing if the entire planet froze up.<br /><br />But maybe I shouldn’t have focused on all those nitpicky things? In any case, the plot was interesting enough to make me curious to find out what happened, and I got through the whole book. I liked the premise but really, those aliens could have and should have wiped out Earth long before the small sections of humans were deployed to stop them… Weird. I won’t be reading the next one, but I enjoyed this enough to give it three stars.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook narrator <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/908077.Edoardo_Ballerini" title="Edoardo Ballerini" rel="nofollow noopener">Edoardo Ballerini</a> rating: 4 stars</b><br /><b>Audiobook narrator <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2826367.Amanda_Leigh_Cobb" title="Amanda Leigh Cobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda Leigh Cobb</a> rating: 3 stars</b><br />Edoardo was good at changing his voice. The other one was ok.</span>

<div id="review_2734759185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63095317-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534275881p2/63095317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734759185?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/63095317-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734759185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14223351415527272380">I’ll admit, the reason I decided to try my first A.G. Riddle book (The Atlantis Gene) was because I was born in the RDU area and wanted to back up a fellow North Carolinian. However, the reason I read my second, third, fourth etc.. A.G. Riddle book was because I was just hooked. He always reels you in immediately. His characters are incredibly likable and you feel a kinship to them by chapter 3, you just want them to win! <br/>This book is no different. I loved the characters but I also loved the plo</span>
  <span id="freeText14223351415527272380" style="display:none">I’ll admit, the reason I decided to try my first A.G. Riddle book (The Atlantis Gene) was because I was born in the RDU area and wanted to back up a fellow North Carolinian. However, the reason I read my second, third, fourth etc.. A.G. Riddle book was because I was just hooked. He always reels you in immediately. His characters are incredibly likable and you feel a kinship to them by chapter 3, you just want them to win! <br />This book is no different. I loved the characters but I also loved the plot. In a day when we are so concerned with our world heating up more and faster than ever, Mr. Riddle turns it around completely. What if the opposite were happening? What if our solar energy started to weaken? In Winter World, a team is sent into space to try to find what is causing the sun’s power failure, which is causing a virtually instant ice age around the globe (which of course is leading to an extinction level event). What they find is anything but natural! As usual, I thoroughly enjoyed the science, characters and Mr.Riddle’s vision of extraterrestrials and our first dealings with them . I always think writing GOOD science fiction has to be one of the most difficult genres to write because you have to be incredibly knowledgeable in math, sciences, technology, etc. Then you have to make up believable future tech &amp; other non-human species using that knowledge all without sounding totally ridiculous . Mr. Riddle has it down though! I can’t wait for book 2! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14223351415527272380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2715704411" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2715704411" />
    <a title="Jerry Mount" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13864984-jerry-mount"><img alt="Jerry Mount" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368662004p2/13864984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2715704411?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerry Mount" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerry Mount" href="/user/show/13864984-jerry-mount">Jerry Mount</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2715704411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1682591770073571543">I've really liked all of Mr. Riddle's other books, but this one fell short for me. The premise of the book was quite good, but the execution was a bit weak. The book is named The Long Winter, but the actual "winter apocalypse" and eradication of most of mankind is not well covered at all. It is used mostly for set up to a space combat story. Sort of a mash-up of the movies Armageddon, Independence Day, and the Day After Tomorrow. Most of the book is spent on the male protagonist, who is made out</span>
  <span id="freeText1682591770073571543" style="display:none">I've really liked all of Mr. Riddle's other books, but this one fell short for me. The premise of the book was quite good, but the execution was a bit weak. The book is named The Long Winter, but the actual "winter apocalypse" and eradication of most of mankind is not well covered at all. It is used mostly for set up to a space combat story. Sort of a mash-up of the movies Armageddon, Independence Day, and the Day After Tomorrow. Most of the book is spent on the male protagonist, who is made out to be a super-genius, superhero, Great Leader, etc. I didn't get this character at all. The heroic female protagonist was well presented at first, then was turned into basically a whiny girlfriend. There are a lot of holes in the time frames, the science and technology, the strategies, and the motives of the antagonists. I just couldn't accept most of what I was reading. The big secret reveal near the end didn't pay off for me at all. I also think the romance should have been dialed way back, or eliminated completely. The winter apocalypse and it's effect on mankind should have been greatly expanded. The main character could have been more human and less all-knowing and omnipotent. Other characters could have been a much bigger part of the story. I don't think I'll be continuing this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1682591770073571543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2867120458" />
    <a title="Kenneth J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39506055-kenneth-j"><img alt="Kenneth J" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2867120458?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kenneth J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kenneth J" href="/user/show/39506055-kenneth-j">Kenneth J</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2867120458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16949318802570893763">An odd book. Sure it's sci-fi with an end of the world as we know it theme but.......<br/>My biggest issue is that time and space appear to be irrelevant. Events seem occur out of the blue. Travel across earth happens in the blink of an eye. Engineering developments are "pulled out of hat" and always work.<br/>AS some other reviewers have noted, the pace of the book seems to be that of a screenplay or even a diary. It's written from a POV perspective of only two characters which is a little disconcerting </span>
  <span id="freeText16949318802570893763" style="display:none">An odd book. Sure it's sci-fi with an end of the world as we know it theme but.......<br />My biggest issue is that time and space appear to be irrelevant. Events seem occur out of the blue. Travel across earth happens in the blink of an eye. Engineering developments are "pulled out of hat" and always work.<br />AS some other reviewers have noted, the pace of the book seems to be that of a screenplay or even a diary. It's written from a POV perspective of only two characters which is a little disconcerting given the number of characters in the story.<br />Maybe I was expecting more but book was enjoyable. I just found myself asking too many times, "how did they pull that off" as well as wondering where in time is the book set. Is it contemporary time, 22nd century time or a hundred thousand years in the future.<br />Yes, I will read book 2 if only because I want to see how the author handles his characters as the planet becomes an ice ball.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16949318802570893763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4eV3RYQ30YdzBwZV9BGlv6ghoZjmbk7xdCAwZOWb2scdEwkSyOBVE/Dr+KsQ8wXBleSmC1HSZOt554pCD6lgwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ivjOIr566xjUBiL/7hlIeVTH0fjOg2SLLL7ZSiJSvkh2DrB18q1vjFfq3AEK++gHaQLWa3k/TpEheWNsyGAETg==')})
  }
//]]>

In the course of nearly five years of recorded interviews Frank Sheeran confessed to Charles Brandt that he handled more than twenty-five hits for the mob, and for his friend Hoffa. Sheeran learned to kill in the U.S. Army, where he saw an astonishing 411 days of active combat duty in Italy during World War II. After returning home he became a hustler and hit man, working for legendary crime boss Russell Bufalino. Eventually he would rise to a position of such prominence that in a RICO suit then-U.S. Attorney Rudy Giuliani would name him as one of only two non-Italians on a list of 26 top mob figures. When Bufalino ordered Sheeran to kill Hoffa, he did the deed, knowing that if he had refused he would have been killed himself. Sheeran\'s important and fascinating story includes new information on other famous murders, and provides rare insight to a chapter in American history. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14778881768899735058">A.G. Riddle spent ten years starting internet companies before retiring to pursue his true passion: writing fiction.<br/><br/>His debut novel, The Atlantis Gene, is the first book in The Origin Mystery, the trilogy that has sold a million copies in the US, is being translated into 19 languages, and is in development at CBS Films to be a major motion picture. The trilogy will be in bookstores (in hardcover a</span>
  <span id="freeText14778881768899735058" style="display:none">A.G. Riddle spent ten years starting internet companies before retiring to pursue his true passion: writing fiction.<br /><br />His debut novel, The Atlantis Gene, is the first book in The Origin Mystery, the trilogy that has sold a million copies in the US, is being translated into 19 languages, and is in development at CBS Films to be a major motion picture. The trilogy will be in bookstores (in hardcover and paperback) around the world in 2015.<br /><br />His recently released fourth novel, Departure, follows the survivors of a flight that takes off in 2014 and crash-lands in a changed world. The hardcover will be published by HarperCollins in the fall of 2015, and 20th Century Fox is developing the novel for a feature film. <br /><br />Riddle grew up in a small town in the US (Boiling Springs, North Carolina) and graduated from UNC-Chapel Hill. During his sophomore year of college, he started his first company with a childhood friend. He currently lives in Florida with his wife, who endures his various idiosyncrasies in return for being the first to read his new novels.<br /><br />No matter where he is, or what's going on, he tries his best to set aside time every day to answer emails and messages from readers. You can reach him at: ag@agriddle.com<br /><br /><br />** For a sneak peek at new novels, free stories, and more, join the email list at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.agriddle.com/email">www.agriddle.com/email</a><br /><br /><br />If you don't want to miss any Riddle news, you can:<br /><br />Like the A.G. Riddle Facebook page: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://facebook.com/agriddle">facebook.com/agriddle</a><br /><br />Follow A.G. Riddle on Twitter: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/riddlist">twitter.com/riddlist</a><br /><br /><br />For more, please visit:<br />AGRiddle.com<br /><br />* * *<br /><br /></span>
